[^5]: 8 (long) cubits is approximately 14 feet or 4.3 meters. ( 40:9)
[^6]: 2 (long) cubits is approximately 3.5 feet or 1.1 meters. ( 40:9)
[^7]: 10 (long) cubits is approximately 17.5 feet or 5.3 meters. ( 40:11)
[^8]: 13 (long) cubits is approximately 22.75 feet or 6.9 meters. ( 40:11)
[^9]: 25 (long) cubits is approximately 43.75 feet or 13.3 meters; also in verses 21, 25, 29, 30, 33, and 36. ( 40:13)
[^10]: 60 (long) cubits is approximately 105 feet or 32 meters. ( 40:14)
[^11]: 50 (long) cubits is approximately 87.5 feet or 26.7 meters; also in verses 21, 25, 29, 33, and 36. ( 40:15)
[^12]: Or gateposts or jambs or projecting walls; here and throughout Ezekiel 40 and 41. ( 40:16)
[^13]: 100 (long) cubits is approximately 175 feet or 53.3 meters; also in verses 23, 27, and 47. ( 40:19)
[^14]: The porticoes were approximately 43.75 feet long and 8.75 feet deep (13.3 meters long and 2.7 meters deep). ( 40:30)
[^15]: LXX and Vulgate (see also verses 26, 31, and 34); Hebrew jambs or dividing wall ( 40:37)
[^16]: Hebrew at the jambs ( 40:38)
[^17]: The tables were approximately 2.6 feet in length and width, and 1.75 feet high (79.2 centimeters in length and width, and 53.3 centimeters high). ( 40:42)
[^18]: Or shelves ( 40:43)
[^19]: A handbreadth is approximately 2.9 inches or 7.4 centimeters long. ( 40:43)
[^20]: LXX; Hebrew within the inner court were chambers for the singers ( 40:44)
[^21]: LXX; Hebrew the east gateway ( 40:44)
[^22]: LXX; the gateway was approximately 24.5 feet or 7.5 meters wide, with sidewalls approximately 5.25 feet or 1.6 meters wide on either side. Hebrew The width of the gateway was three cubits on either side. ( 40:48)
[^23]: 20 (long) cubits is approximately 35 feet or 10.7 meters. ( 40:49)
[^24]: LXX; 12 (long) cubits is approximately 21 feet or 6.4 meters; Hebrew eleven cubits deep; that is, approximately 19.25 feet or 5.9 meters. ( 40:49)
[^25]: LXX; Hebrew and steps led up to it ( 40:49)

### Chapter 41

#### Inside the Temple
**v1** Then the man brought me into the outer sanctuary and measured the side pillars to be six cubits wide [^1] on each side. [^2]
**v2** The width of the entrance was ten cubits, [^3] and the sides of the entrance were five cubits [^4] on each side. He also measured the length of the outer sanctuary to be forty cubits, and the width to be twenty cubits. [^5]

**v3** And he went into the inner sanctuary and measured the side pillars at the entrance to be two cubits wide. [^6] The entrance was six cubits wide, and the walls on each side were seven cubits wide. [^7]
**v4** Then he measured the room adjacent to the inner sanctuary [^8] to be twenty cubits long and twenty cubits wide. [^9] And he said to me, "This is the Most Holy Place. [^10]"
#### Outside the Temple

**v5** Next he measured the wall of the temple to be six cubits thick, and the width of each side room around the temple was four cubits. [^11]
**v6** The side rooms were arranged one above another in three levels of thirty rooms each. There were ledges all around the wall of the temple to serve as supports for the side rooms, so that the supports would not be fastened into the wall of the temple itself.
**v7** The side rooms surrounding the temple widened at each successive level, because the structure surrounding the temple ascended by stages corresponding to the narrowing of the temple wall as it rose upward. And so a stairway went up from the lowest story to the highest, through the middle one.

**v8** I saw that the temple had a raised base all around it, forming the foundation of the side rooms. It was the full length of a rod, six long cubits.
**v9** The outer wall of the side rooms was five cubits thick, and the open area between the side rooms of the temple
**v10** and the outer chambers was twenty cubits wide all around the temple.
**v11** The side rooms opened into this area, with one entrance on the north and another on the south. The open area was five cubits wide all around.

**v12** Now the building that faced the temple courtyard on the west was seventy cubits wide, [^12] and the wall of the building was five cubits thick all around, with a length of ninety cubits. [^13]

**v13** Then he measured the temple to be a hundred cubits long, [^14] and the temple courtyard and the building with its walls were also a hundred cubits long.
**v14** The width of the temple courtyard on the east, including the front of the temple, was a hundred cubits.
#### The Interior Structures

**v15** Next he measured the length of the building facing the temple courtyard at the rear of the temple, including its galleries on each side; it was a hundred cubits. The outer sanctuary, the inner sanctuary, and the porticoes facing the court,
**v16** as well as the thresholds and the beveled windows and the galleries all around with their three levels opposite the threshold, were overlaid with wood on all sides. They were paneled from the ground to the windows, and the windows were covered.

**v17** In the space above the outside of the entrance to the inner sanctuary on all the walls, spaced evenly around the inner and outer sanctuary,
**v18** were alternating carved cherubim and palm trees. Each cherub had two faces:
**v19** the face of a man was toward the palm tree on one side, and the face of a young lion was toward the palm tree on the other side. They were carved all the way around the temple.
**v20** Cherubim and palm trees were carved on the wall of the outer sanctuary from the floor to the space above the entrance.

**v21** The outer sanctuary had a rectangular doorframe, and the doorframe of the sanctuary was similar.

**v22** There was an altar of wood three cubits high and two cubits square. [^15] Its corners, base, and sides were of wood. And the man told me, "This is the table that is before the LORD."

**v23** Both the outer sanctuary and the inner sanctuary had double doors,
**v24** and each door had two swinging panels. There were two panels for one door and two for the other.
**v25** Cherubim and palm trees like those on the walls were carved on the doors of the outer sanctuary, and there was a wooden canopy outside, on the front of the portico.
**v26** There were beveled windows and palm trees on the sidewalls of the portico. The side rooms of the temple also had canopies.
[^1]: 6 (long) cubits is approximately 10.5 feet or 3.2 meters; also in verses 3, 5, and 8. ( 41:1)
[^2]: One Hebrew manuscript and LXX; most Hebrew manuscripts on each side—the width of the tent ( 41:1)
[^3]: 10 (long) cubits is approximately 17.5 feet or 5.3 meters. ( 41:2)
[^4]: 5 (long) cubits is approximately 8.75 feet or 2.7 meters; also in verses 9, 11, and 12. ( 41:2)
[^5]: The outer sanctuary was approximately 70 feet long and 35 feet wide (21.3 meters long and 10.7 meters wide). ( 41:2)
[^6]: 2 (long) cubits is approximately 3.5 feet or 1.1 meters. ( 41:3)
[^7]: 7 (long) cubits is approximately 12.25 feet or 3.7 meters. ( 41:3)
[^8]: Or the length of the inner sanctuary ( 41:4)
[^9]: The room was approximately 35 feet long and 35 feet wide (10.7 meters long and 10.7 meters wide). ( 41:4)
[^10]: Or the Holy of Holies ( 41:4)
[^11]: 4 (long) cubits is approximately 7 feet or 2.1 meters. ( 41:5)
[^12]: 70 (long) cubits is approximately 122.5 feet or 37.3 meters. ( 41:12)
[^13]: 90 (long) cubits is approximately 157.5 feet or 48 meters. ( 41:12)
[^14]: 100 (long) cubits is approximately 175 feet or 53.3 meters; similarly in verses 14 and 15. ( 41:13)
[^15]: Or long; the altar was approximately 5.25 feet high and 3.5 feet square (1.6 meters high and 1.1 meters square) ( 41:22)

### Chapter 42

#### Chambers for the Priests
**v1** Then the man led me out northward into the outer court, and he brought me to the group of chambers opposite the temple courtyard and the outer wall on the north side.
**v2** The building with the door facing north was a hundred cubits long and fifty cubits wide. [^1]
**v3** Gallery faced gallery in three levels opposite the twenty cubits [^2] that belonged to the inner court and opposite the pavement that belonged to the outer court.

**v4** In front of the chambers was an inner walkway ten cubits wide and a hundred cubits long. [^3] Their doors were on the north.

**v5** Now the upper chambers were smaller because the galleries took more space from the chambers on the lower and middle floors of the building.
**v6** For they were arranged in three stories, and unlike the courts, they had no pillars. So the upper chambers were set back further than the lower and middle floors.
**v7** An outer wall in front of the chambers was fifty cubits long and ran parallel to the chambers and the outer court.
**v8** For the chambers on the outer court were fifty cubits long, while those facing the temple were a hundred cubits long.
**v9** And below these chambers was the entrance on the east side as one enters them from the outer court.

**v10** On the south side [^4] along the length of the wall of the outer court were chambers adjoining the courtyard and opposite the building,
**v11** with a passageway in front of them, just like the chambers that were on the north. They had the same length and width, with similar exits and dimensions.
**v12** And corresponding to the doors of the chambers that were facing south, there was a door in front of the walkway that was parallel to the wall extending eastward.

**v13** Then the man said to me, "The north and south chambers facing the temple courtyard are the holy chambers where the priests who approach the LORD will eat the most holy offerings. There they will place the most holy offerings—the grain offerings, the sin offerings, and the guilt offerings—for the place is holy.
**v14** Once the priests have entered the holy area, they must not go out into the outer court until they have left behind the garments in which they minister, for these are holy. They are to put on other clothes before they approach the places that are for the people."
#### The Outer Measurements

**v15** Now when the man had finished measuring the interior of the temple area, he led me out by the gate that faced east, and he measured the area all around:

**v16** With a measuring rod he measured the east side to be five hundred cubits long. [^5]

**v17** He measured the north side to be five hundred cubits long.

**v18** He measured the south side to be five hundred cubits long.

**v19** And he came around and measured the west side to be five hundred cubits long.

**v20** So he measured the area on all four sides. It had a wall all around, five hundred cubits long and five hundred cubits wide, to separate the holy from the common.
[^1]: The building was approximately 175 feet long and 87.5 feet wide (53.3 meters long and 26.7 meters wide). ( 42:2)
[^2]: 20 (long) cubits is approximately 35 feet or 10.7 meters. ( 42:3)
[^3]: LXX. The walkway was approximately 17.5 feet wide and 175 feet long (5.3 meters wide and 53.3 meters long). Hebrew ten cubits wide and a cubit long. ( 42:4)
[^4]: LXX; Hebrew east side ( 42:10)
[^5]: See LXX; five hundred cubits from verse 17 LXX and implied in verses 16, 18, 19, and 20 is approximately 875 feet or 266.7 meters in length. Hebrew five hundred reeds, with the measuring reed round about, that is approximately 5,250 feet or 1,600 meters; similarly in verses 17, 18, 19, and 20. ( 42:16)

### Chapter 43

#### The Glory of the LORD Returns to the Temple
**v1** Then the man brought me back to the gate that faces east,
**v2** and I saw the glory of the God of Israel coming from the east. His voice was like the roar of many waters, and the earth shone with His glory.

**v3** The vision I saw was like the vision I had seen when He came [^1] to destroy the city and like the visions I had seen by the River Kebar. I fell facedown,
**v4** and the glory of the LORD entered the temple through the gate facing east.
**v5** Then the Spirit lifted me up and brought me into the inner court, and the glory of the LORD filled the temple.

**v6** While the man was standing beside me, I heard someone speaking to me from inside the temple,
**v7** and He said to me, "Son of man, this is the place of My throne and the place for the soles of My feet, where I will dwell among the Israelites forever. The house of Israel will never again defile My holy name—neither they nor their kings—by their prostitution and by the funeral offerings [^2] for their kings at their deaths. [^3]
**v8** When they placed their threshold next to My threshold and their doorposts beside My doorposts, with only a wall between Me and them, they defiled My holy name by the abominations they committed. Therefore I have consumed them in My anger.
**v9** Now let them remove far from Me their prostitution and the funeral offerings for their kings, and I will dwell among them forever.

**v10** As for you, son of man, describe the temple to the people of Israel, so that they may be ashamed of their iniquities. Let them measure the plan,
**v11** and if they are ashamed [^4] of all they have done, then make known to them the design of the temple—its arrangement and its exits and entrances—its whole design along with all its statutes, forms, and laws. Write it down in their sight, so that they may keep its complete design and all its statutes and may carry them out.

**v12** This is the law of the temple: All its surrounding territory on top of the mountain will be most holy. Yes, this is the law of the temple.
#### The Altar of Sacrifice

**v13** These are the measurements of the altar in long cubits [^5](a cubit and a handbreadth): Its gutter shall be a cubit deep and a cubit wide, with a rim of one span [^6] around its edge.And this is the height of the altar:
**v14** The space from the gutter on the ground to the lower ledge shall be two cubits, and the ledge one cubit wide. [^7] The space from the smaller ledge to the larger ledge shall be four cubits, and the ledge one cubit wide. [^8]

**v15** The altar hearth shall be four cubits high, and four horns shall project upward from the hearth.
**v16** The altar hearth shall be square at its four corners, twelve cubits long and twelve cubits wide. [^9]
**v17** The ledge shall also be square, fourteen cubits long and fourteen cubits wide, [^10] with a rim of half a cubit [^11] and a gutter of a cubit all around it. The steps of the altar shall face east."

**v18** Then He said to me: "Son of man, this is what the Lord GOD says: 'These are the statutes for the altar on the day it is constructed, so that burnt offerings may be sacrificed on it and blood may be splattered on it:
**v19** You are to give a young bull from the herd as a sin offering to the Levitical priests who are of the family of Zadok, who approach Me to minister before Me, declares the Lord GOD.
**v20** You are to take some of its blood and put it on the four horns of the altar, on the four corners of the ledge, and all around the rim; thus you will cleanse the altar and make atonement for it.
**v21** Then you are to take away the bull for the sin offering and burn it in the appointed part of the temple area outside the sanctuary.

**v22** On the second day you are to present an unblemished male goat as a sin offering, and the altar is to be cleansed as it was with the bull.
**v23** When you have finished the purification, you are to present a young, unblemished bull and an unblemished ram from the flock.
**v24** You must present them before the LORD; the priests are to sprinkle salt on them and sacrifice them as a burnt offering to the LORD.

**v25** For seven days you are to provide a male goat daily for a sin offering; you are also to provide a young bull and a ram from the flock, both unblemished.
**v26** For seven days the priests are to make atonement for the altar and cleanse it; so they shall consecrate it. [^12]
**v27** At the end of these days, from the eighth day on, the priests are to present your burnt offerings and peace offerings on the altar. Then I will accept you, declares the Lord GOD.'"
[^1]: Some Hebrew manuscripts and Vulgate; most Hebrew manuscripts when I came ( 43:3)
[^2]: Or the monuments; also in verse 9 ( 43:7)
[^3]: Or for their kings on their high places ( 43:7)
[^4]: Hebrew; LXX and Vulgate and they will be ashamed ( 43:11)
[^5]: The long cubit, about 21 inches or 53.3 centimeters, is the basic unit for linear measurement throughout Ezekiel 40–48. ( 43:13)
[^6]: One span is approximately 9 inches or 22.9 centimeters. ( 43:13)
[^7]: The space was to be approximately 3.5 feet (1.1 meters), and the ledge was to be approximately 1.75 feet wide (53.3 centimeters wide). ( 43:14)
[^8]: The space was to be approximately 7 feet (2.1 meters), and the ledge was to be approximately 1.75 feet wide (53.3 centimeters wide). ( 43:14)
[^9]: 12 (long) cubits is approximately 21 feet or 6.4 meters. ( 43:16)
[^10]: 14 (long) cubits is approximately 24.5 feet or 7.5 meters. ( 43:17)
[^11]: A half cubit is approximately 10.5 inches or 26.7 centimeters. ( 43:17)
[^12]: Hebrew fill its hand ( 43:26)

### Chapter 44

#### The East Gate Assigned to the Prince
**v1** The man then brought me back to the outer gate of the sanctuary that faced east, but it was shut.
**v2** And the LORD said to me, "This gate is to remain shut. It shall not be opened, and no man shall enter through it, because the LORD, the God of Israel, has entered through it. Therefore it will remain shut.
**v3** Only the prince himself may sit inside the gateway to eat in the presence of the LORD. He must enter by way of the portico of the gateway and go out the same way."

**v4** Then the man brought me to the front of the temple by way of the north gate. I looked and saw the glory of the LORD filling His temple, and I fell facedown.
**v5** The LORD said to me: "Son of man, pay attention; look carefully with your eyes and listen closely with your ears to everything I tell you concerning all the statutes and laws of the house of the LORD. Take careful note of the entrance to the temple, along with all the exits of the sanctuary.
#### Reproof of the Levites

**v6** Tell the rebellious house of Israel that this is what the Lord GOD says: 'I have had enough of all your abominations, O house of Israel.
**v7** In addition to all your other abominations, you brought in foreigners uncircumcised in both heart and flesh to occupy My sanctuary; you defiled My temple when you offered My food—the fat and the blood; you broke My covenant.
**v8** And you have not kept charge of My holy things, but have appointed others to keep charge of My sanctuary for you.'

**v9** This is what the Lord GOD says: No foreigner uncircumcised in heart and flesh may enter My sanctuary—not even a foreigner who lives among the Israelites.

**v10** Surely the Levites who wandered away from Me when Israel went astray, and who wandered away from Me after their idols, will bear the consequences of their iniquity.
**v11** Yet they shall be ministers in My sanctuary, having charge of the gates of the temple and ministering there. They shall slaughter the burnt offerings and other sacrifices for the people and stand before them to minister to them.

**v12** Because they ministered before their idols and became a stumbling block of iniquity to the house of Israel, therefore I swore with an uplifted hand concerning them that they would bear the consequences of their iniquity, declares the Lord GOD.
**v13** They must not approach Me to serve Me as priests or come near any of My holy things or the most holy things. They will bear the shame of the abominations they have committed.
**v14** Yet I will appoint them to keep charge of all the work for the temple and everything to be done in it.
#### The Duties of the Priests

**v15** But the Levitical priests, who are descended from Zadok and who kept charge of My sanctuary when the Israelites went astray from Me, are to approach Me to minister before Me. They will stand before Me to offer Me fat and blood, declares the Lord GOD.
**v16** They alone shall enter My sanctuary and draw near to My table to minister before Me. They will keep My charge.

**v17** When they enter the gates of the inner court, they are to wear linen garments; they must not wear anything made of wool when they minister at the gates of the inner court or inside the temple.
**v18** They are to wear linen turbans on their heads and linen undergarments around their waists. They must not wear anything that makes them perspire.

**v19** When they go out to the outer court, to the people, they are to take off the garments in which they have ministered, leave them in the holy chambers, and dress in other clothes so that they do not transmit holiness to the people with their garments.

**v20** They must not shave their heads or let their hair grow long, but must carefully trim their hair.
**v21** No priest may drink wine before he enters the inner court.
**v22** And they shall not marry a widow or a divorced woman, but must marry a virgin of the descendants of the house of Israel, or a widow of a priest.
**v23** They are to teach My people the difference between the holy and the common and show them how to discern between the clean and the unclean.

**v24** In any dispute, they shall officiate as judges and judge according to My ordinances. They must keep My laws and statutes regarding all My appointed feasts, and they must keep My Sabbaths holy.

**v25** A priest must not defile himself by going near a dead person. However, for a father, a mother, a son, a daughter, a brother, or an unmarried sister, he may do so,
**v26** and after he is cleansed, he must count off seven days for himself.
**v27** And on the day he goes into the sanctuary, into the inner court, to minister in the sanctuary, he must present his sin offering, declares the Lord GOD.

**v28** In regard to their inheritance, I am their inheritance. You are to give them no possession in Israel, for I am their possession.

**v29** They shall eat the grain offerings, the sin offerings, and the guilt offerings. Everything in Israel devoted to the LORD will belong to them.
**v30** The best of all the firstfruits and of every contribution from all your offerings will belong to the priests. You are to give your first batch of dough to the priest, so that a blessing may rest upon your homes.
**v31** The priests may not eat any bird or animal found dead or torn by wild beasts.
### Chapter 45

#### Consecration of the Land
**v1** "When you divide the land by lot as an inheritance, you are to set aside a portion for the LORD, a holy portion of the land 25,000 cubits long and 20,000 cubits wide. [^1] This entire tract of land will be holy.

**v2** Within this area there is to be a section for the sanctuary 500 cubits square, [^2] with 50 cubits [^3] around it for open land.

**v3** From this holy portion, you are to measure off a length of 25,000 cubits and a width of 10,000 cubits, [^4] and in it will be the sanctuary, the Most Holy Place. [^5]
**v4** It will be a holy portion of the land to be used by the priests who minister in the sanctuary, who draw near to minister before the LORD. It will be a place for their houses, as well as a holy area for the sanctuary.

**v5** An adjacent area 25,000 cubits long and 10,000 cubits wide shall belong to the Levites who minister in the temple; it will be their possession for towns in which to live. [^6]

**v6** As the property of the city, you are to set aside an area 5,000 cubits wide and 25,000 cubits long, [^7] adjacent to the holy district. It will belong to the whole house of Israel.
#### The Prince's Portion

**v7** Now the prince will have the area bordering each side of the area formed by the holy district and the property of the city, extending westward from the western side and eastward from the eastern side, running lengthwise from the western boundary to the eastern boundary and parallel to one of the tribal portions.
**v8** This land will be his possession in Israel.And My princes will no longer oppress My people, but will give the rest of the land to the house of Israel according to their tribes.
**v9** For this is what the Lord GOD says: 'Enough, O princes of Israel! Cease your violence and oppression, and do what is just and right. Stop dispossessing My people, declares the Lord GOD.'
#### Honest Scales

**v10** You must use honest scales, a just ephah, [^8] and a just bath. [^9]

**v11** The ephah and the bath shall be the same quantity so that the bath will contain a tenth of a homer, and the ephah a tenth of a homer; the homer will be the standard measure for both. [^10]

**v12** The shekel will consist of twenty gerahs. [^11] Twenty shekels plus twenty-five shekels plus fifteen shekels will equal one mina. [^12]
#### Offerings and Feasts

**v13** This is the contribution you are to offer: a sixth of an ephah from each homer of wheat, and a sixth of an ephah from each homer of barley. [^13]
**v14** The prescribed portion of oil, measured by the bath, is a tenth of a bath from each cor [^14](a cor consists of ten baths or one homer, since ten baths are equivalent to a homer).
**v15** And one sheep shall be given from each flock of two hundred from the well-watered pastures of Israel. These are for the grain offerings, burnt offerings, and peace offerings, to make atonement for the people, declares the Lord GOD.

**v16** All the people of the land must participate in this contribution for the prince in Israel.
**v17** And it shall be the prince's part to provide the burnt offerings, grain offerings, and drink offerings for the feasts, New Moons, and Sabbaths—for all the appointed feasts of the house of Israel. He will provide the sin offerings, [^15] grain offerings, burnt offerings, and peace offerings to make atonement for the house of Israel.

**v18** This is what the Lord GOD says: 'On the first day of the first month you are to take a young bull without blemish and purify the sanctuary.
**v19** And the priest is to take some of the blood from the sin offering and put it on the doorposts of the temple, on the four corners of the ledge of the altar, and on the gateposts of the inner court.
**v20** You must do the same thing on the seventh day of the month for anyone who strays unintentionally or in ignorance. In this way you will make atonement for the temple.

**v21** On the fourteenth day of the first month you are to observe the Passover, a feast of seven days, during which unleavened bread shall be eaten.
**v22** On that day the prince shall provide a bull as a sin offering for himself and for all the people of the land.
**v23** Each day during the seven days of the feast, he shall provide seven bulls and seven rams without blemish as a burnt offering to the LORD, along with a male goat for a sin offering.
**v24** He shall also provide as a grain offering an ephah for each bull and an ephah for each ram, along with a hin of olive oil for each ephah of grain. [^16]
**v25** During the seven days of the feast that begins on the fifteenth day of the seventh month, [^17] he is to make the same provision for sin offerings, burnt offerings, grain offerings, and oil.'
[^1]: LXX; the holy portion was to be approximately 8.3 miles long and 6.6 miles wide (13.3 kilometers long and 10.7 kilometers wide). Hebrew 25,000 cubits long and 10,000 wide. See also verses 3 and 5 and Ezekiel 48:9. ( 45:1)
[^2]: 500 (long) cubits is approximately 875 feet or 266.7 meters. ( 45:2)
[^3]: 50 (long) cubits is approximately 87.5 feet or 26.7 meters. ( 45:2)
[^4]: The portion was to be approximately 8.3 miles long and 3.3 miles wide (13.3 kilometers long and 5.3 kilometers wide); similarly in verse 5. ( 45:3)
[^5]: Or the Holy of Holies ( 45:3)
[^6]: LXX; Hebrew their possession, twenty chambers ( 45:5)
[^7]: The property of the city was to be approximately 1.7 miles wide and 8.3 miles long (2.7 kilometers wide and 13.3 kilometers long). ( 45:6)
[^8]: An ephah is a dry measure of approximately 20 dry quarts or 22 liters. ( 45:10)
[^9]: A bath was a liquid measure of approximately 5.8 gallons or 22 liters. ( 45:10)
[^10]: A homer was a dry measure of approximately 6.24 bushels or 220 liters; also in verses 13 and 14. ( 45:11)
[^11]: 20 gerahs is equivalent to one shekel (approximately 0.4 ounces or 11.4 grams). ( 45:12)
[^12]: That is, 60 shekels total; elsewhere, the common mina was 50 shekels. Sixty shekels weighed approximately 1.5 pounds or 683.8 grams. ( 45:12)
[^13]: That is, a sixtieth of the harvest of wheat and of barley; a sixth of an ephah was approximately 3.3 dry quarts or 3.7 liters. ( 45:13)
[^14]: That is, one percent of one's oil; a tenth of a bath was approximately 2.3 quarts or 2.2 liters. ( 45:14)
[^15]: Or purification offerings; also in verses 19, 22, 23, and 25 ( 45:17)
[^16]: Literally a hin of oil for each ephah; that is, approximately 0.97 gallons or 3.67 liters of oil for each ephah of grain ( 45:24)
[^17]: That is, Sukkot, the autumn feast of pilgrimage to Jerusalem; also translated as the Feast of Booths or the Feast of Shelters and originally called the Feast of Ingathering (see Exodus 23:16 and Exodus 34:22). ( 45:25)

### Chapter 46

#### The Prince's Offerings
**v1** "This is what the Lord GOD says: 'The gate of the inner court that faces east must be kept shut during the six days of work, but on the Sabbath day and on the day of the New Moon it shall be opened.
**v2** The prince is to enter from the outside through the portico of the gateway and stand by the gatepost, while the priests sacrifice his burnt offerings and peace offerings. He is to bow in worship at the threshold of the gate and then depart, but the gate must not be shut until evening.
**v3** On the Sabbaths and New Moons the people of the land are also to bow in worship before the LORD at the entrance to that gateway.

**v4** The burnt offering that the prince presents to the LORD on the Sabbath day shall be six unblemished male lambs and an unblemished ram.
**v5** The grain offering with the ram shall be one ephah, [^1] and the grain offering with the lambs shall be as much as he is able, along with a hin of oil per ephah.
**v6** On the day of the New Moon he shall offer a young, unblemished bull, six lambs, and a ram without blemish.
**v7** He is to provide a grain offering of an ephah with the bull, an ephah with the ram, and as much as he is able with the lambs, along with a hin of oil per ephah.
**v8** When the prince enters, he shall go in through the portico of the gateway, and he shall go out the same way.

**v9** When the people of the land come before the LORD at the appointed feasts, whoever enters by the north gate to worship must go out by the south gate, and whoever enters by the south gate must go out by the north gate. No one is to return through the gate by which he entered, but each must go out by the opposite gate.

**v10** When the people enter, the prince shall go in with them, and when they leave, he shall leave.
**v11** At the festivals and appointed feasts, the grain offering shall be an ephah with a bull, an ephah with a ram, and as much as one is able to give with the lambs, along with a hin of oil per ephah.

**v12** When the prince makes a freewill offering to the LORD, whether a burnt offering or a peace offering, the gate facing east must be opened for him. He is to offer his burnt offering or peace offering just as he does on the Sabbath day. Then he shall go out, and the gate must be closed after he goes out.

**v13** And you shall provide an unblemished year-old lamb as a daily burnt offering to the LORD; you are to offer it every morning.
**v14** You are also to provide with it every morning a grain offering of a sixth of an ephah [^2] with a third of a hin of oil [^3] to moisten the fine flour—a grain offering to the LORD. This is a permanent statute.
**v15** Thus they shall provide the lamb, the grain offering, and the oil every morning as a regular burnt offering.'

**v16** This is what the Lord GOD says: 'If the prince gives a gift to any of his sons as an inheritance, it will belong to his descendants. It will become their property by inheritance.
**v17** But if he gives a gift from his inheritance to one of his servants, it will belong to that servant until the year of freedom; then it will revert to the prince. His inheritance belongs only to his sons; it shall be theirs.

**v18** The prince must not take any of the inheritance of the people by evicting them from their property. He is to provide an inheritance for his sons from his own property, so that none of My people will be displaced from his property.'"
#### The Courts for Boiling and Baking

**v19** Then the man brought me through the entrance at the side of the gate into the holy chambers facing north, which belonged to the priests, and he showed me a place there at the far western end
**v20** and said to me, "This is the place where the priests shall boil the guilt offering and the sin offering, and where they shall bake the grain offering, so that they do not bring them into the outer court and transmit holiness to the people."

**v21** Then he brought me into the outer court and led me around to its four corners, and I saw a separate court in each of its corners.
**v22** In the four corners of the outer court there were enclosed courts, each forty cubits long and thirty cubits wide. [^4] Each of the four corner areas had the same dimensions.
**v23** Around the inside of each of the four courts was a row of masonry with ovens built at the base of the walls on all sides.

**v24** And he said to me, "These are the kitchens where those who minister at the temple will cook the sacrifices offered by the people."
[^1]: An ephah is approximately 20 dry quarts or 22 liters (probably about 38.3 pounds or 17.4 kilograms of grain); also in verses 7 and 11. ( 46:5)
[^2]: A sixth of an ephah is approximately 3.3 dry quarts or 3.7 liters (probably about 4.2 pounds or 1.9 kilograms of flour). ( 46:14)
[^3]: Or a third of a hin of olive oil; that is, approximately 1.3 quarts or 1.2 liters ( 46:14)
[^4]: The enclosed courts were approximately 70 feet long and 52.5 feet wide (21.3 meters long and 16 meters wide). ( 46:22)

### Chapter 47

#### Waters from under the Temple
**v1** Then the man brought me back to the entrance of the temple, and I saw water flowing from under the threshold of the temple toward the east (for the temple faced east). The water was coming down from under the south side of the temple, south of the altar.

**v2** Next he brought me out through the north gate and led me around the outside to the outer gate facing east, and there I saw the water trickling out from the south side.

**v3** As the man went eastward with a measuring line in his hand, he measured off a thousand cubits [^1] and led me through ankle-deep water.

**v4** Then he measured off a thousand cubits and led me through knee-deep water.Again he measured a thousand cubits and led me through waist-deep water.

**v5** Once again he measured off a thousand cubits, but now it was a river that I could not cross, because the water had risen and was deep enough for swimming—a river that could not be crossed on foot.

**v6** "Son of man, do you see this?" he asked. Then he led me back to the bank of the river.

**v7** When I arrived, I saw a great number of trees along both banks of the river.
**v8** And he said to me, "This water flows out to the eastern region and goes down into the Arabah. When it empties into the Dead Sea, [^2] the water there becomes fresh. [^3]
**v9** Wherever the river flows, there will be swarms of living creatures and a great number of fish, because it flows there and makes the waters fresh; so wherever the river flows, everything will flourish.

**v10** Fishermen will stand by the shore; from En-gedi to En-eglaim they will spread their nets to catch fish of many kinds, like the fish of the Great Sea. [^4]

**v11** But the swamps and marshes will not become fresh; they will be left for salt.

**v12** Along both banks of the river, fruit trees of all kinds will grow. Their leaves will not wither, and their fruit will not fail. Each month they will bear fruit, because the water from the sanctuary flows to them. Their fruit will be used for food and their leaves for healing."
#### The Borders of the Land

**v13** This is what the Lord GOD says: "These are the boundaries by which you are to divide the land as an inheritance among the twelve tribes of Israel; Joseph shall receive two portions. [^5]
**v14** You are to divide it equally among them. Because I swore with an uplifted hand to give it to your forefathers, this land will fall to you as an inheritance.

**v15** This shall be the boundary of the land:On the north side it will extend from the Great Sea by way of Hethlon through Lebo-hamath to Zedad,
**v16** Berothah, and Sibraim [^6](which is on the border between Damascus and Hamath), as far as Hazer-hatticon, which is on the border of Hauran.
**v17** So the border will run from the Sea to Hazar-enan, along the northern border of Damascus, with the territory of Hamath to the north. This will be the northern boundary.

**v18** On the east side the border will run between Hauran and Damascus, along the Jordan between Gilead and the land of Israel, to the Eastern Sea and as far as Tamar. [^7] This will be the eastern boundary.

**v19** On the south side it will run from Tamar to the waters of Meribath-kadesh, and along the Brook of Egypt [^8] to the Great Sea. This will be the southern boundary.

**v20** And on the west side, the Great Sea will be the boundary up to a point opposite Lebo-hamath. This will be the western boundary.

**v21** You are to divide this land among yourselves according to the tribes of Israel.
**v22** You shall allot it as an inheritance for yourselves and for the foreigners who dwell among you and who have children. You are to treat them as native-born Israelites; along with you, they shall be allotted an inheritance among the tribes of Israel.
**v23** In whatever tribe a foreigner dwells, you are to assign his inheritance there," declares the Lord GOD.
[^1]: 1,000 (long) cubits is approximately 1,750 feet or 533.4 meters. ( 47:3)
[^2]: That is, the Dead Sea ( 47:8)
[^3]: Hebrew is healed; similarly in verses 9 and 11 ( 47:8)
[^4]: That is, the Mediterranean Sea; also in verses 15, 19, and 20 ( 47:10)
[^5]: Since Levi had no portion, Joseph's sons Ephraim and Manasseh received land as two tribes. ( 47:13)
[^6]: LXX; MT 15...through Lebo to Zedad, 16 Hamath, Berothah, and Sibraim ( 47:16)
[^7]: See Syriac; that is, of Israel, to the Dead Sea and as far as Tamar; Hebrew of Israel. And along the Eastern Sea you are to measure. ( 47:18)
[^8]: Hebrew does not include of Egypt. ( 47:19)

### Chapter 48

#### The Portions for the Tribes
**v1** "Now these are the names of the tribes:At the northern frontier, Dan will have one portion bordering the road of Hethlon to Lebo-hamath and running on to Hazar-enan on the border of Damascus with Hamath to the north, and extending from the east side to the west side.

**v2** Asher will have one portion bordering the territory of Dan from east to west.

**v3** Naphtali will have one portion bordering the territory of Asher from east to west.

**v4** Manasseh will have one portion bordering the territory of Naphtali from east to west.

**v5** Ephraim will have one portion bordering the territory of Manasseh from east to west.

**v6** Reuben will have one portion bordering the territory of Ephraim from east to west.

**v7** Judah will have one portion bordering the territory of Reuben from east to west.
#### The Portions for the Priests and Levites

**v8** Bordering the territory of Judah, from east to west, will be the portion you are to set apart. It will be 25,000 cubits wide, [^1] and the length of a tribal portion from east to west. In the center will be the sanctuary.

**v9** The special portion you set apart to the LORD shall be 25,000 cubits long and 10,000 cubits wide. [^2]

**v10** This will be the holy portion for the priests. It will be 25,000 cubits long on the north side, 10,000 cubits wide on the west side, 10,000 cubits wide on the east side, and 25,000 cubits long on the south side. In the center will be the sanctuary of the LORD.
**v11** It will be for the consecrated priests, the descendants of Zadok, who kept My charge and did not go astray as the Levites did when the Israelites went astray.
**v12** It will be a special portion for them set apart from the land, a most holy portion [^3] adjacent to the territory of the Levites.

**v13** Bordering the territory of the priests, the Levites shall have an area 25,000 cubits long and 10,000 cubits wide. The whole length will be 25,000 cubits, and the width 10,000 cubits.
**v14** They must not sell or exchange any of it, and they must not transfer this best part of the land, for it is holy to the LORD.
#### The Common Portion

**v15** The remaining area, 5,000 cubits [^4] wide and 25,000 cubits long, will be for common use by the city, for houses, and for pastureland. The city will be in the center of it
**v16** and will have these measurements: 4,500 cubits [^5] on the north side, 4,500 cubits on the south side, 4,500 cubits on the east side, and 4,500 cubits on the west side.

**v17** The pastureland of the city will extend 250 cubits [^6] to the north, 250 cubits to the south, 250 cubits to the east, and 250 cubits to the west.

**v18** The remainder of the length bordering the holy portion and running adjacent to it will be 10,000 cubits on the east side and 10,000 cubits on the west side. Its produce will supply food for the workers of the city.
**v19** The workers of the city who cultivate it will come from all the tribes of Israel.

**v20** The entire portion will be a square, 25,000 cubits by 25,000 cubits. You are to set apart the holy portion, along with the city property.
#### The Portion for the Prince

**v21** The remaining area on both sides of the holy portion and of the property of the city will belong to the prince. He will own the land adjacent to the tribal portions, extending eastward from the 25,000 cubits of the holy district toward the eastern border, and westward from the 25,000 cubits to the western border. And in the center of them will be the holy portion and the sanctuary of the temple.

**v22** So the Levitical property and the city property will lie in the center of the area belonging to the prince—the area between the borders of Judah and Benjamin.
#### The Portions for the Remaining Tribes

**v23** As for the rest of the tribes:Benjamin will have one portion extending from the east side to the west side.

**v24** Simeon will have one portion bordering the territory of Benjamin from east to west.

**v25** Issachar will have one portion bordering the territory of Simeon from east to west.

**v26** Zebulun will have one portion bordering the territory of Issachar from east to west.

**v27** And Gad will have one portion bordering the territory of Zebulun from east to west.

**v28** The southern border of Gad will run from Tamar to the waters of Meribath-kadesh, then along the Brook of Egypt [^7] and out to the Great Sea. [^8]
**v29** This is the land you are to allot as an inheritance to the tribes of Israel, and these will be their portions," declares the Lord GOD.
#### The City Gates and Dimensions

**v30** "These will be the exits of the city:Beginning on the north side, which will be 4,500 cubits long,
**v31** the gates of the city will be named after the tribes of Israel. On the north side there will be three gates: the gate of Reuben, the gate of Judah, and the gate of Levi.

**v32** On the east side, which will be 4,500 cubits long, there will be three gates: the gate of Joseph, the gate of Benjamin, and the gate of Dan.

**v33** On the south side, which will be 4,500 cubits long, there will be three gates: the gate of Simeon, the gate of Issachar, and the gate of Zebulun.

**v34** And on the west side, which will be 4,500 cubits long, there will be three gates: the gate of Gad, the gate of Asher, and the gate of Naphtali.

**v35** The perimeter of the city will be 18,000 cubits, [^9] and from that day on the name of the city will be:THE LORD IS THERE. [^10]"
[^1]: 25,000 (long) cubits is approximately 8.3 miles or 13.3 kilometers; also in verses 9, 10, 13, 15, 20, and 21. ( 48:8)
[^2]: 10,000 (long) cubits is approximately 3.3 miles or 5.3 kilometers; also in verses 10, 13, and 18. ( 48:9)
[^3]: Or a Most Holy Place ( 48:12)
[^4]: 5,000 (long) cubits is approximately 1.7 miles or 2.7 kilometers. ( 48:15)
[^5]: 4,500 (long) cubits is approximately 1.5 miles or 2.4 kilometers; also in verses 30, 32, 33, and 34. ( 48:16)
[^6]: 250 (long) cubits is approximately 437.5 feet or 133.4 meters. ( 48:17)
[^7]: Hebrew does not include of Egypt. ( 48:28)
[^8]: That is, the Mediterranean Sea ( 48:28)
[^9]: 18,000 (long) cubits is approximately 6 miles or 9.6 kilometers. ( 48:35)
[^10]: Hebrew YHWH Shammah ( 48:35)

## Daniel

### Chapter 1

#### Daniel Removed to Babylon
**v1** In the third year of the reign of Jehoiakim king of Judah, Nebuchadnezzar king of Babylon came to Jerusalem and besieged it.
**v2** And the Lord delivered into his hand Jehoiakim king of Judah, along with some of the articles from the house of God. He carried these off to the land of Shinar, [^1] to the house of his god, where he put them in the treasury of his god.

**v3** Then the king ordered Ashpenaz, the chief of his court officials, to bring in some Israelites from the royal family [^2] and the nobility—
**v4** young men without blemish, handsome, gifted in all wisdom, knowledgeable, quick to understand, and qualified to serve in the king's palace—and to teach them the language and literature of the Chaldeans. [^3]

**v5** The king assigned them daily provisions of the royal food and wine. They were to be trained for three years, after which they were to enter the king's service.

**v6** Among these young men were some from Judah: Daniel, Hananiah, Mishael, and Azariah.
**v7** The chief official gave them new names: To Daniel he gave the name Belteshazzar; to Hananiah, Shadrach; to Mishael, Meshach; and to Azariah, Abednego.
#### Daniel's Faithfulness

**v8** But Daniel made up his mind that he would not defile himself with the king's food or wine. So he asked the chief official for permission not to defile himself.

**v9** Now God had granted Daniel favor and compassion from the chief official,
**v10** but he said to Daniel, "I fear my lord the king, who has assigned your food and drink. For why should he see your faces looking thinner than those of the other young men your age? You would endanger my head before the king!"

**v11** Then Daniel said to the steward whom the chief official had appointed over Daniel, Hananiah, Mishael, and Azariah,
**v12** "Please test your servants for ten days. Let us be given only vegetables to eat and water to drink.
**v13** Then compare our appearances with those of the young men who are eating the royal food, and deal with your servants according to what you see."

**v14** So he consented to this and tested them for ten days.
**v15** And at the end of ten days, they looked healthier and better nourished than all the young men who were eating the king's food.
**v16** So the steward continued to withhold their choice food and the wine they were to drink, and he gave them vegetables instead.
#### Daniel's Wisdom

**v17** To these four young men God gave knowledge and understanding in every kind of literature and wisdom. And Daniel had insight into all kinds of visions and dreams.

**v18** Now at the end of the time specified by the king, the chief official presented them to Nebuchadnezzar.
**v19** And the king spoke with them, and among all the young men he found no one equal to Daniel, Hananiah, Mishael, and Azariah. So they entered the king's service.

**v20** In every matter of wisdom and understanding about which the king consulted them, he found them ten times better than all the magicians and enchanters in his entire kingdom.
**v21** And Daniel remained there until the first year of King Cyrus.
[^1]: That is, Babylonia ( 1:2)
[^2]: Hebrew from the seed of the kingdom ( 1:3)
[^3]: That is, the Babylonians ( 1:4)

### Chapter 2

#### Nebuchadnezzar's Troubling Dream
**v1** In the second year of his reign, Nebuchadnezzar had dreams that troubled his spirit, and sleep escaped him.
**v2** So the king gave orders to summon the magicians, enchanters, sorcerers, and astrologers [^1] to explain his dreams. When they came and stood before the king,
**v3** he said to them, "I have had a dream, and my spirit is anxious to understand it."

**v4** Then the astrologers answered the king in Aramaic, [^2]"O king, may you live forever! Tell your servants the dream, and we will give the interpretation."

**v5** The king replied to the astrologers, "My word is final: If you do not tell me the dream and its interpretation, you will be cut into pieces and your houses will be reduced to rubble.
**v6** But if you tell me the dream and its interpretation, you will receive from me gifts and rewards and great honor. So tell me the dream and its interpretation."

**v7** They answered a second time, "Let the king tell the dream to his servants, and we will give the interpretation."

**v8** The king replied, "I know for sure that you are stalling for time because you see that my word is final.
**v9** If you do not tell me the dream, there is only one decree for you. You have conspired to speak before me false and fraudulent words, hoping the situation will change. Therefore tell me the dream, and I will know that you can give me its interpretation."

**v10** The astrologers answered the king, "No one on earth can do what the king requests! No king, however great and powerful, has ever asked anything like this of any magician, enchanter, or astrologer.
**v11** What the king requests is so difficult that no one can tell it to him except the gods, whose dwelling is not with mortals."

**v12** This response made the king so angry and furious that he gave orders to destroy all the wise men of Babylon.
**v13** So the decree went out that the wise men were to be executed, and men went to look for Daniel and his friends to execute them.
#### The Dream Revealed to Daniel

**v14** When Arioch, the commander of the king's guard, went out to execute the wise men of Babylon, Daniel responded with discretion and tact.
**v15** "Why is the decree from the king so harsh?" he asked.Then Arioch explained the situation to Daniel.
**v16** So Daniel went in and asked the king to give him some time, so that he could give him the interpretation.

**v17** Then Daniel returned to his house and explained the matter to his friends Hananiah, Mishael, and Azariah,
**v18** urging them to plead for mercy from the God of heaven concerning this mystery, so that Daniel and his friends would not be killed with the rest of the wise men of Babylon.

**v19** During the night, the mystery was revealed to Daniel in a vision, and he blessed the God of heaven
**v20** and declared: "Blessed be the name of God forever and ever, for wisdom and power belong to Him.
**v21** He changes the times and seasons; He removes kings and establishes them.He gives wisdom to the wiseand knowledge to the discerning.
**v22** He reveals the deep and hidden things; He knows what lies in darkness, and light dwells with Him.
**v23** To You, O God of my fathers, I give thanks and praise, because You have given mewisdom and power.And now You have made known to mewhat we have requested, for You have made known to usthe dream of the king."
#### Daniel Interprets the Dream

**v24** Therefore Daniel went to Arioch, whom the king had appointed to destroy the wise men of Babylon, and said to him, "Do not execute the wise men of Babylon! Bring me before the king, and I will give him the interpretation."

**v25** Arioch hastily brought Daniel before the king and said to him, "I have found a man among the exiles from Judah who will tell the king the interpretation."

**v26** The king responded to Daniel, whose name was Belteshazzar, "Are you able to tell me what I saw in the dream, as well as its interpretation?"

**v27** Daniel answered the king, "No wise man, enchanter, medium, or magician can explain to the king the mystery of which he inquires.
**v28** But there is a God in heaven who reveals mysteries, and He has made known to King Nebuchadnezzar what will happen in the latter days. Your dream and the visions that came into your mind as you lay on your bed were these:

**v29** As you lay on your bed, O king, your thoughts turned to the future, and the Revealer of Mysteries made known to you what will happen.
**v30** And to me this mystery has been revealed, not because I have more wisdom than any man alive, but in order that the interpretation might be made known to the king, and that you may understand the thoughts of your mind.

**v31** As you, O king, were watching, a great statue [^3] appeared. A great and dazzling statue stood before you, and its form was awesome.
**v32** The head of the statue was pure gold, its chest and arms were silver, its belly and thighs were bronze,
**v33** its legs were iron, and its feet were part iron and part clay.

**v34** As you watched, a stone was cut out, [^4] but not by human hands. It struck the statue on its feet of iron and clay, and crushed them.
**v35** Then the iron, clay, bronze, silver, and gold were shattered and became like chaff on the threshing floor in summer. The wind carried them away, and not a trace of them could be found. But the stone that had struck the statue became a great mountain and filled the whole earth.

**v36** This was the dream; now we will tell the king its interpretation.

**v37** You, O king, are the king of kings, to whom the God of heaven has given sovereignty, power, strength, and glory.
**v38** Wherever the sons of men or beasts of the field or birds of the air dwell, He has given them into your hand and has made you ruler over them all. You are that head of gold.

**v39** But after you, there will arise another kingdom, inferior to yours.Next, a third kingdom, one of bronze, will rule the whole earth.

**v40** Finally, there will be a fourth kingdom as strong as iron; for iron shatters and crushes all things, and like iron that crushes all things, it will shatter and crush all the others.
**v41** And just as you saw that the feet and toes were made partly of fired clay and partly of iron, so this will be a divided kingdom, yet some of the strength of iron will be in it—just as you saw the iron mixed with clay.
**v42** And as the toes of the feet were partly iron and partly clay, so this kingdom will be partly strong and partly brittle.
**v43** As you saw the iron mixed with clay, so the peoples [^5] will mix with one another but will not hold together any more than iron mixes with clay.

**v44** In the days of those kings, the God of heaven will set up a kingdom that will never be destroyed, nor will it be left to another people. It will shatter all these kingdoms and bring them to an end, but will itself stand forever.
**v45** And just as you saw a stone being cut out of the mountain without human hands, and it shattered the iron, bronze, clay, silver, and gold, so the great God has told the king what will happen in the future.The dream is true, and its interpretation is trustworthy."
#### Nebuchadnezzar Promotes Daniel

**v46** At this, King Nebuchadnezzar fell on his face, paid homage to Daniel, and ordered that an offering and incense be presented to him.
**v47** The king said to Daniel, "Your God is truly the God of gods and Lord of kings, the Revealer of Mysteries, since you were able to reveal this mystery."

**v48** Then the king promoted Daniel and gave him many generous gifts. He made him ruler over the entire province of Babylon and chief administrator over all the wise men of Babylon.
**v49** And at Daniel's request, the king appointed Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego to manage the province of Babylon, while Daniel remained in the king's court.
[^1]: Or Chaldeans; also in verses 4, 5, and 10 ( 2:2)
[^2]: The original text from this point of Daniel 2:4 through Daniel 7:28 is in Aramaic. ( 2:4)
[^3]: Or image; here and through the rest of Daniel 2 ( 2:31)
[^4]: LXX cut out from a mountain ( 2:34)
[^5]: Aramaic the seed of men ( 2:43)

### Chapter 3

#### Nebuchadnezzar's Golden Statue
**v1** King Nebuchadnezzar made a golden statue [^1] sixty cubits high and six cubits wide, [^2] and he set it up on the plain of Dura in the province of Babylon.
**v2** Then King Nebuchadnezzar sent word to assemble the satraps, prefects, governors, advisers, treasurers, judges, magistrates, and all the other officials of the provinces to attend the dedication of the statue he had set up.

**v3** So the satraps, prefects, governors, advisers, treasurers, judges, magistrates, and all the rulers of the provinces assembled for the dedication of the statue that King Nebuchadnezzar had set up, and they stood before it.

**v4** Then the herald loudly proclaimed, "O people of every nation and language, this is what you are commanded:
**v5** As soon as you hear the sound of the horn, flute, zither, lyre, harp, pipes, and all kinds of music, [^3] you must fall down and worship the golden statue that King Nebuchadnezzar has set up.
**v6** And whoever does not fall down and worship will immediately be thrown into the blazing fiery furnace."

**v7** Therefore, as soon as all the people heard the sound of the horn, flute, zither, lyre, harp, and all kinds of music, the people of every nation and language would fall down and worship the golden statue that King Nebuchadnezzar had set up.
#### Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego Accused

**v8** At this time some astrologers [^4] came forward and maliciously accused the Jews,
**v9** saying to King Nebuchadnezzar, "O king, may you live forever!
**v10** You, O king, have issued a decree that everyone who hears the sound of the horn, flute, zither, lyre, harp, pipes, and all kinds of music must fall down and worship the golden statue,
**v11** and that whoever does not fall down and worship will be thrown into the blazing fiery furnace.
**v12** But there are some Jews you have appointed to manage the province of Babylon—Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego—who have ignored you, O king, and have refused to serve your gods or worship the golden statue you have set up."

**v13** Then Nebuchadnezzar, furious with rage, summoned Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego. So these men were brought before the king,
**v14** and Nebuchadnezzar said to them, "Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego, is it true that you do not serve my gods or worship the golden statue I have set up?
**v15** Now when you hear the sound of the horn, flute, zither, lyre, harp, pipes, and all kinds of music, if you are ready to fall down and worship the statue I have made, very good. But if you refuse to worship, you will be thrown at once into the blazing fiery furnace. Then what god will be able to deliver you from my hands?"

**v16** Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego replied to the king, "O Nebuchadnezzar, we have no need to answer you in this matter.
**v17** If the God whom we serve exists, then He is able [^5] to deliver us from the blazing fiery furnace and from your hand, O king.
**v18** But even if He does not, let it be known to you, O king, that we will not serve your gods or worship the golden statue you have set up."
#### The Fiery Furnace

**v19** At this, Nebuchadnezzar was filled with rage, and the expression on his face changed toward Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego. He gave orders to heat the furnace seven times hotter than usual,
**v20** and he commanded some mighty men of valor in his army to tie up Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego and throw them into the blazing fiery furnace.

**v21** So they were tied up, wearing robes, trousers, turbans, and other clothes, and they were thrown into the blazing fiery furnace.

**v22** The king's command was so urgent and the furnace so hot that the fiery flames killed the men who carried up Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego.
**v23** And these three men, Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego, firmly bound, fell into the blazing fiery furnace.

**v24** Suddenly King Nebuchadnezzar jumped up in amazement and asked his advisers, "Did we not throw three men, firmly bound, into the fire?""Certainly, O king," they replied.

**v25** "Look!" he exclaimed. "I see four men, unbound and unharmed, walking around in the fire—and the fourth looks like a son of the gods! [^6]"

**v26** Then Nebuchadnezzar approached the door of the blazing fiery furnace and called out, "Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego, servants of the Most High God, come out!" So Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego came out of the fire,
**v27** and when the satraps, prefects, governors, and royal advisers had gathered around, they saw that the fire had no effect on the bodies of these men. Not a hair of their heads was singed, their robes were unaffected, and there was no smell of fire on them.

**v28** Nebuchadnezzar declared, "Blessed be the God of Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego, who has sent His angel [^7] and delivered His servants who trusted in Him. They violated the king's command and risked their lives rather than serve or worship any god except their own God.
**v29** Therefore I decree that the people of any nation or language who say anything offensive against the God of Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego will be cut into pieces and their houses reduced to rubble. For there is no other god who can deliver in this way."

**v30** Then the king promoted Shadrach, Meshach, and Abednego in the province of Babylon.
[^1]: Or image; here and throughout Daniel 3 ( 3:1)
[^2]: The statue was approximately 90 feet high and 9 feet wide (27.4 meters high and 2.7 meters wide). ( 3:1)
[^3]: The precise identification of some musical instruments in this chapter is uncertain. ( 3:5)
[^4]: Or Chaldeans ( 3:8)
[^5]: Or If this be so, then the God whom we serve is able ( 3:17)
[^6]: Or like the Son of God ( 3:25)
[^7]: Or Angel ( 3:28)

### Chapter 4

#### Nebuchadnezzar Confesses God's Kingdom
**v1** King Nebuchadnezzar, To the people of every nation and language who dwell in all the earth:May your prosperity be multiplied.
**v2** I am pleased to declare the signs and wonders that the Most High God has performed for me.

**v3** How great are His signs, how mighty His wonders!His kingdom is an eternal kingdom; His dominion endures from generation to generation.
#### Nebuchadnezzar's Dream of a Great Tree

**v4** I, Nebuchadnezzar, was at ease in my house and flourishing in my palace.
**v5** I had a dream, and it frightened me; while I was in my bed, the images and visions in my mind alarmed me.
**v6** So I issued a decree that all the wise men of Babylon be brought before me to interpret the dream for me.
**v7** When the magicians, enchanters, astrologers, [^1] and diviners came in, I told them the dream, but they could not interpret it for me.

**v8** But at last, into my presence came Daniel (whose name is Belteshazzar after the name of my god, and in whom is the spirit of the holy gods). And I told him the dream:
**v9** "O Belteshazzar, chief of the magicians, I know that the spirit of the holy gods is in you and that no mystery baffles you. So explain to me the visions I saw in my dream, and their interpretation.
**v10** In these visions of my mind as I was lying in bed, I saw this come to pass:There was a tree in the midst of the land, and its height was great.
**v11** The tree grew large and strong; its top reached the sky, and it was visibleto the ends of the earth.
**v12** Its leaves were beautiful, its fruit was abundant, and upon it was food for all.Under it the beasts of the field found shelter, in its branches the birds of the air nested, and from it every creature was fed.

**v13** As I lay on my bed, I also saw in the visions of my mind a watcher, [^2] a holy one, coming down from heaven.
**v14** He called out in a loud voice: 'Cut down the tree and chop off its branches; strip off its leaves and scatter its fruit.Let the beasts flee from under it, and the birds from its branches.
**v15** But leave the stump with its roots in the ground, with a band of iron and bronze around it, in the tender grass of the field.Let him be drenched with the dew of heavenand graze with the beasts on the grass of the earth.
**v16** Let his mind be changed from that of a man, and let him be given the mind of a beasttill seven times pass him by.
**v17** This decision is the decree of the watchers, the verdict declared by the holy ones, so that the living will knowthat the Most High rules over the kingdom of mankindand gives it to whom He wishes, setting over it the lowliest of men.'

**v18** This is the dream that I, King Nebuchadnezzar, saw. Now, Belteshazzar, tell me the interpretation, because none of the wise men of my kingdom can interpret it for me. But you are able, because the spirit of the holy gods is in you."
#### Daniel Interprets the Second Dream

**v19** For a time, Daniel, who was also known as Belteshazzar, was perplexed, and his thoughts alarmed him.So the king said, "Belteshazzar, do not let the dream or its interpretation alarm you.""My lord," replied Belteshazzar, "may the dream apply to those who hate you, and its interpretation to your enemies!

**v20** The tree you saw that grew large and strong, whose top reached the sky and was visible to all the earth,
**v21** whose foliage was beautiful and whose fruit was abundant, providing food for all, under which the beasts of the field lived, and in whose branches the birds of the air nested—
**v22** you, O king, are that tree! For you have become great and strong; your greatness has grown to reach the sky, and your dominion extends to the ends of the earth.

**v23** And you, O king, saw a watcher, a holy one, coming down from heaven and saying: 'Cut down the tree and destroy it, but leave the stump with its roots in the ground, with a band of iron and bronze around it, in the tender grass of the field.Let him be drenched with the dew of heaven, and graze with the beasts of the fieldtill seven times pass him by.'

**v24** This is the interpretation, O king, and this is the decree that the Most High has issued against my lord the king:

**v25** You will be driven away from mankind, and your dwelling will be with the beasts of the field. You will feed on grass like an ox and be drenched with the dew of heaven, and seven times shall pass you by, until you acknowledge that the Most High rules over the kingdom of mankind and gives it to whom He wishes.

**v26** As for the command to leave the stump of the tree with its roots, your kingdom will be restored to you as soon as you acknowledge that Heaven rules.
**v27** Therefore, may my advice be pleasing to you, O king. Break away from your sins by doing what is right, and from your iniquities by showing mercy to the oppressed. Perhaps there will be an extension of your prosperity."
#### The Second Dream Fulfilled

**v28** All this happened to King Nebuchadnezzar.
**v29** Twelve months later, as he was walking on the roof of the royal palace of Babylon,
**v30** the king exclaimed, "Is this not Babylon the Great, which I myself have built as a royal residence by the might of my power and for the glory of my majesty?"

**v31** While the words were still in the king's mouth, a voice came from heaven: "It is decreed to you, King Nebuchadnezzar, that the kingdom has departed from you.
**v32** You will be driven away from mankind to live with the beasts of the field, and you will feed on grass like an ox. And seven times will pass you by, until you acknowledge that the Most High rules over the kingdom of mankind and gives it to whom He wishes."

**v33** At that moment the sentence against Nebuchadnezzar was fulfilled. He was driven away from mankind. He ate grass like an ox, and his body was drenched with the dew of heaven, until his hair grew like the feathers of an eagle and his nails like the claws of a bird.
#### Nebuchadnezzar Restored

**v34** But at the end of those days I, Nebuchadnezzar, looked up to heaven, and my sanity was restored to me. Then I praised the Most High, and I honored and glorified Him who lives forever: "For His dominion is an everlasting dominion, and His kingdom endures from generation to generation.
**v35** All the peoples of the earthare counted as nothing, and He does as He pleaseswith the army of heavenand the peoples of the earth.There is no one who can restrain His handor say to Him, 'What have You done?'"

**v36** At the same time my sanity was restored, my honor and splendor returned to me for the glory of my kingdom. My advisers and nobles sought me out, and I was restored to my throne, and surpassing greatness was added to me.
**v37** Now I, Nebuchadnezzar, praise and exalt and glorify the King of heaven, for all His works are true and all His ways are just. And He is able to humble those who walk in pride.
[^1]: Or Chaldeans ( 4:7)
[^2]: Or an angelic watcher or a messenger; also in verses 17 and 23 ( 4:13)

### Chapter 5

#### Belshazzar's Feast
**v1** Later, [^1] King Belshazzar held a great feast for a thousand of his nobles, and he drank wine with them.
**v2** Under the influence of the wine, Belshazzar gave orders to bring in the gold and silver vessels that Nebuchadnezzar his father [^2] had taken from the temple in Jerusalem, so that the king could drink from them, along with his nobles, his wives, and his concubines.

**v3** Thus they brought in the gold vessels that had been taken from the temple, the house of God in Jerusalem, and the king drank from them, along with his nobles, his wives, and his concubines.
**v4** As they drank the wine, they praised their gods of gold and silver, bronze and iron, wood and stone.
#### The Handwriting on the Wall

**v5** At that moment the fingers of a human hand appeared and wrote on the plaster of the wall, near the lampstand in the royal palace. As the king watched the hand that was writing,
**v6** his face grew pale and his thoughts so alarmed him that his hips gave way and his knees knocked together.

**v7** The king called out for the enchanters, astrologers, [^3] and diviners to be brought in, and he said to these wise men of Babylon, "Whoever reads this inscription and tells me its interpretation will be clothed in purple and have a gold chain placed around his neck, and he will be made the third highest ruler in the kingdom."

**v8** So all the king's wise men came in, but they could not read the inscription or interpret it for him.
**v9** Then King Belshazzar became even more terrified, his face grew even more pale, and his nobles were bewildered.

**v10** Hearing the outcry of the king and his nobles, the queen [^4] entered the banquet hall. "O king, may you live forever!" she said. "Do not let your thoughts terrify you, or your face grow pale.
**v11** There is a man in your kingdom who has the spirit of the holy gods in him. In the days of your father he was found to have insight, intelligence, and wisdom like that of the gods.Your father, King Nebuchadnezzar, appointed him chief of the magicians, enchanters, astrologers, and diviners. Your own father, the king,
**v12** did this because Daniel, the one he named Belteshazzar, was found to have an extraordinary spirit, as well as knowledge, understanding, and the ability to interpret dreams, explain riddles, and solve difficult problems. Summon Daniel, therefore, and he will give you the interpretation."
#### Daniel Interprets the Handwriting

**v13** So Daniel was brought before the king, who asked him, "Are you Daniel, one of the exiles my father the king brought from Judah?
**v14** I have heard that the spirit of the gods is in you, and that you have insight, intelligence, and extraordinary wisdom.

**v15** Now the wise men and enchanters were brought before me to read this inscription and interpret it for me, but they could not give its interpretation.
**v16** But I have heard about you, that you are able to give interpretations and solve difficult problems. Therefore, if you can read this inscription and give me its interpretation, you will be clothed in purple and have a gold chain placed around your neck, and you will be made the third highest ruler in the kingdom."

**v17** In response, Daniel said to the king, "You may keep your gifts for yourself and give your rewards to someone else. Nevertheless, I will read the inscription for the king and interpret it for him.
**v18** As for you, O king, the Most High God gave your father Nebuchadnezzar sovereignty and greatness, glory and honor.
**v19** Because of the greatness that He bestowed on him, the people of every nation and language trembled in fear before him. He killed whom he wished and kept alive whom he wished; he exalted whom he wished and humbled whom he wished.

**v20** But when his heart became arrogant and his spirit was hardened with pride, he was deposed from his royal throne, and his glory was taken from him.
**v21** He was driven away from mankind, and his mind was like that of a beast. He lived with the wild donkeys and ate grass like an ox, and his body was drenched with the dew of heaven until he acknowledged that the Most High God rules over the kingdom of mankind, setting over it whom He wishes.

**v22** But you his son, [^5] O Belshazzar, have not humbled your heart, even though you knew all this.
**v23** Instead, you have exalted yourself against the Lord of heaven. The vessels from His house were brought to you, and as you drank wine from them with your nobles, wives, and concubines, you praised your gods of silver and gold, bronze and iron, wood and stone, which cannot see or hear or understand. But you have failed to glorify the God who holds in His hand your very breath and all your ways.
**v24** Therefore He sent the hand that wrote the inscription.

**v25** Now this is the inscription that was written:MENE, MENE, TEKEL, PARSIN.

**v26** And this is the interpretation of the message:MENE [^6] means that God has numbered the days of your reign and brought it to an end.

**v27** TEKEL [^7] means that you have been weighed on the scales and found deficient.

**v28** PERES [^8] means that your kingdom has been divided and given over to the Medes and Persians."

**v29** Then Belshazzar gave the command, and they clothed Daniel in purple, placed a gold chain around his neck, and proclaimed him the third highest ruler in the kingdom.

**v30** That very night Belshazzar king of the Chaldeans [^9] was slain,
**v31** and Darius the Mede received the kingdom at the age of sixty-two.
[^1]: Aramaic does not include Later. Some translators include Many years later to account for the time elapsed, probably about 30 years, since the previous chapter. ( 5:1)
[^2]: Or predecessor or grandfather; also in verses 11, 13, and 18 ( 5:2)
[^3]: Or Chaldeans; also in verse 11 ( 5:7)
[^4]: Or queen mother ( 5:10)
[^5]: Or descendant or successor or grandson ( 5:22)
[^6]: Mene sounds like the Aramaic for numbered. ( 5:26)
[^7]: Tekel sounds like the Aramaic for weighed. ( 5:27)
[^8]: Peres (the singular of Parsin) sounds like the Aramaic for divided and for Persia. ( 5:28)
[^9]: That is, the Babylonians ( 5:30)

### Chapter 6

#### The Plot against Daniel
**v1** Now it pleased Darius to appoint 120 satraps to rule throughout the kingdom,
**v2** and over them three administrators, including Daniel, to whom these satraps were accountable so that the king would not suffer loss.
**v3** Soon, by his extraordinary spirit, Daniel distinguished himself among the administrators and satraps. So the king planned to set him over the whole kingdom.

**v4** Thus the administrators and satraps sought a charge against Daniel concerning the kingdom, but they could find no charge or corruption, because he was trustworthy, and no negligence or corruption was found in him.
**v5** Finally these men said, "We will never find any charge against this Daniel unless we find something against him concerning the law of his God."

**v6** So the administrators and satraps went together to the king and said, "O King Darius, may you live forever!
**v7** All the royal administrators, prefects, satraps, advisers, and governors have agreed that the king should establish an ordinance and enforce a decree that for thirty days anyone who petitions any god or man except you, O king, will be thrown into the den of lions.
**v8** Therefore, O king, establish the decree and sign the document so that it cannot be changed—in accordance with the law of the Medes and Persians, which cannot be repealed."

**v9** Therefore King Darius signed the written decree.
#### Daniel in the Lions' Den

**v10** Now when Daniel learned that the document had been signed, he went into his house, where the windows of his upper room opened toward Jerusalem, and three times a day he got down on his knees, prayed, and gave thanks to his God, just as he had done before.
**v11** Then these men went as a group and found Daniel petitioning and imploring his God.
**v12** So they approached the king and asked about his royal decree: "Did you not sign a decree that for thirty days any man who petitions any god or man except you, O king, will be thrown into the den of lions?" The king replied, "According to the law of the Medes and Persians the order stands, and it cannot be repealed."

**v13** Then they told the king, "Daniel, one of the exiles from Judah, shows no regard for you, O king, or for the decree that you have signed. He still makes his petition three times a day."

**v14** As soon as the king heard this, he was deeply distressed and set his mind on delivering Daniel, and he labored until sundown to rescue him.

**v15** Then the men approached the king together and said to him, "Remember, O king, that by the law of the Medes and Persians no decree or ordinance established by the king can be changed."

**v16** So the king gave the order, and they brought Daniel and threw him into the den of lions.The king said to Daniel, "May your God, whom you serve continually, deliver you!"

**v17** A stone was brought and placed over the mouth of the den, and the king sealed it with his own signet ring and with the rings of his nobles, so that nothing concerning Daniel could be changed.

**v18** Then the king went to his palace and spent the night fasting. No entertainment was brought before him, and sleep fled from him.

**v19** At the first light of dawn, the king got up and hurried to the den of lions.
**v20** When he reached the den, he cried out in a voice of anguish, "O Daniel, servant of the living God, has your God, whom you serve continually, been able to deliver you from the lions?"

**v21** Then Daniel replied, "O king, may you live forever!
**v22** My God sent His angel and shut the mouths of the lions. They have not hurt me, for I was found innocent in His sight, and I have done no wrong against you, O king."

**v23** The king was overjoyed and gave orders to lift Daniel out of the den, and when Daniel was lifted out of the den, no wounds whatsoever were found on him, because he had trusted in his God.

**v24** At the command of the king, the men who had falsely accused Daniel were brought and thrown into the den of lions—they and their children and wives. And before they had reached the bottom of the den, the lions overpowered them and crushed all their bones.
#### Darius Honors God

**v25** Then King Darius wrote to the people of every nation and language throughout the land: "May your prosperity abound.
